Prelude to Debt Moratorium 83

A Reuters dispatch from Washington on the 1st reports that the Senate today discussed the war debt issue, focusing on practical aspects. Democratic Senator Tydings proposed paying off the war debt with a lump sum, saying that Britain only has 75 million US dollars worth of gold, and if the United States does not accept goods, how can Britain repay 40 billion in debt? Even the wisest people would be powerless. Democratic leader Robinson said that President Roosevelt is well aware of the difficulty of collecting debts owed to the United States, but based on various phenomena, the President is now implementing the congressional bill previously passed against the cancellation or modification of war debts to the best of his ability. At the same time, Democrat Rini stated in the House of Representatives that the proposed tax bill would give the President the power to conclude reciprocal tariff agreements, and that these agreements could be implemented once announced, without allowing the Senate to veto them. Rini's words can be seen as a prelude to the London war debt negotiations and possible moratorium measures.

Washington's False Teeth

Shipped to Chicago Expo for Display 84

A Reuters dispatch from Chicago reports that the false teeth of the first President of the United States, George Washington, will soon arrive here for display in the Hall of Scientific Progress of a Century of Progress Exposition. They are contained in a steel box 18 inches square and 3 feet 6 inches high, equipped with multiple insurance locks. The box is inlaid with shatterproof glass and will be nailed to the artificial stone floor in the hall and weighed down with iron blocks. Exposition officials have also requested that the military authorities dispatch a group of soldiers dressed in colonial uniforms to guard the box, in order to honor the first commander of the US Army. The teeth are carved from ivory and joined with gold brackets, hinges, and springs, representing a relic from before the profession of dentistry became specialized. Washington repeatedly mentioned his teeth in his diaries and correspondence. This material is helpful to historians, artists, and anecdote writers. Modern people often discuss Washington's mouth shape, which was strained by his false teeth, and there are various ridiculous legends about Washington's false teeth, all of which have been denied by historians studying this issue.

Progress of Ceasefire Agreement Signing (Reached)

Both Armies Have Been Ordered to Withdraw 85

Acceptance of Military Zones Following Shanghai Method

A special dispatch from Beiping reports that the Sino-Japanese ceasefire agreement was formally signed at Tanggu yesterday (31st) at 11:10 AM. The Great Wall conflict, which had lasted for more than two months, has completely ended, and the peace movement, which had been running for many days, has declared its success. The details of the process and subsequent arrangements are recorded below:

Initial Contact 86

The Sino-Japanese peace movement began with Yoshizawa's visit to China. Although there were several twists and turns, it gradually became concrete due to various efforts. All solutions were discussed in Shanghai before, and the opinions of both parties were quite close. Later, the situation in which the Japanese army threatened the situation in Tianjin deteriorated, and on the 22nd of last month, Japanese acting ambassador Nakayama was ordered to contact us to discuss four principles. The peace talks, which were on the verge of a stalemate, took a sharp turn for the better. Afterwards, both parties continued to proceed according to the four principles, and a solution was agreed upon in Miyun to implement a ceasefire. Then, formal representatives were sent to Tanggu to hold a formal meeting.

List of Representatives 87

The list of representatives from both sides is as follows: The chief representative on the Chinese side was Lieutenant General Xiong Bin, chief advisor of the Military Branch; the staff included Major General Qian Zongze, advisor of the Military Branch; advisor Lei Shourong; Colonel Staff Officer Xu Yanmou (i.e., Xu Zuyi); councilors Yin Rugeng and Li Zeyi; and Colonel Zhang Xiguang, chief of staff of the First Army Corps. On the Japanese side, the chief representative was Major General Gangcun Ningji, deputy chief of staff of the Kwantung Army; the staff included Colonel Kita Seiichi of the Infantry; Naval Attaché Lieutenant Colonel Nagatsu Hishige of the Infantry; Staff Officer Major Kawano Etsujiro of the Division; Staff Officer Major Sato Saburo of the Artillery; Sato Moto Tetsuguma of the Infantry; Staff Officer Captain Okabe Hideichi of the Cavalry; interpreter Hayashi Izumi Kenjiro; aide-de-camp Captain Ito Akira of the Artillery; and Military Staff Officer Captain Shizukusa Yukinori of the Engineer Corps. The participating members included Staff Officer Major Ohashi Kumawo of the North China Garrison Army; Naval Attaché Lieutenant Sato Haru Kiyoichi of the Embassy; and Secretary Nakayama Shoichi of the Embassy.

Tanggu Meeting 88

After the meeting location and representatives were determined, representatives from both sides gathered in Tanggu on May 30. The Chinese representatives departed from Beiping by special train at 7:55 AM that morning, with extremely strict security along the way. They paused briefly when passing through Tianjin to meet with Nakamura, the commander of the Japanese Tianjin Garrison. They arrived in Tanggu at 2:40 PM in the afternoon. The Japanese representatives, including Okamura, arrived on a Japanese warship on the evening of the 29th, while staff members such as Nakayama traveled on the special train with our representatives on the 30th. The Chinese representatives stayed at the Yongli Alkali Plant and on the special train, while the Japanese representatives stayed in the Japanese barracks and the Osaka Shosen Company. Tanggu Station was heavily guarded, and the city was also under special security. A curfew was imposed at 8:00 PM. The Chinese representatives went to the Jiuda Fine Salt Company for lunch at around 3:00 PM in the afternoon, and the Japanese representatives were also invited to the banquet. At around 4:00 PM, representatives and all personnel from both China and Japan went to the Osaka Shosen Company to hold the first meeting. They first met each other for ordinary socializing and then immediately convened a meeting that lasted for four hours. All issues were completely agreed upon, and it was decided that the Japanese side would draft the articles of agreement for further discussion the next day. At 9:00 AM on the 31st, the second meeting was held again at the Osaka Shosen Company. First, Japanese representative Okamura presented the terms of the armistice agreement to our representatives, including Xiong Bin, for inspection. After inspecting, our representatives retreated to another room in the conference hall to discuss the terms of the agreement in detail and made slight revisions. They then re-entered the conference hall at 11:00 AM to meet with the Japanese representatives. The Japanese side accepted all the revisions proposed by our side.

Representatives Sign 89

At 11:10 AM, the completed original was written in both Chinese and Japanese, two copies each, and signed by the chief representatives of both sides. The armistice agreement that all parties were watching was thus established. In this meeting, all important issues had been discussed in advance, so no major disputes arose from the beginning of the meeting to the signing, and it was announced to be established in the shortest period of time and in the most favorable circumstances. After the agreement was signed, representatives from both sides held a diplomatic toast ceremony and dispersed. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, the Japanese representatives invited our representatives to an informal discussion, in which they discussed the handling of the rebel army and the security of the demilitarized zone. They dispersed at around 4:00 PM.

Full Text of the Agreement 90

Only five articles of the agreement signed by both parties have been made public by both sides. The rest and the appendices are kept secret. The five articles of the agreement that have been published are as follows: (1) The Chinese army shall withdraw to the area west and south of the line connecting Yanqing, Changping, Gaoliying, Shunyi, Tongzhou, Xianghe, Baodi, Lintingzhen, Ninghe, and Lutai and shall not advance further or engage in any provocative or disruptive actions. (2) The Japanese army may use aircraft or other means to conduct inspections in order to ensure the implementation of the first item. The Chinese side shall provide protection and facilitation. (3) The Japanese army confirms that when the Chinese army has withdrawn to the line agreed upon in the first item, it will not cross the line and continue to pursue, and will automatically return to the line of the Great Wall. (4) The maintenance of security in the area south of the Great Wall line and north and east of the line agreed upon in the first item shall be the responsibility of the Chinese police. (5) This agreement shall take effect immediately after signing.

Demilitarized Zone 91

This agreement is tantamount to an agreement under duress, which cannot be denied. The scope of the demilitarized zone is extremely wide, stretching from Shanhaiguan in the east to Yanqing in the Chahar territory in the west, and as far south as the vicinity of Beiping and Tianjin. The places listed in the agreement, Yanqing is outside the Great Wall, belongs to Chahar, and is about 200 li northwest of Beiping; Changping is 75 li northwest of Beiping, and the PingSui Railway passes through it; Gaoliying is 45 li north of Beiping; Shunyi is 70 li northeast of Beiping; Tongzhou is 45 li east of Beiping; Xianghe is more than 100 li southeast of Beiping, 60 li from Tongzhou; Baodi is 170 li southeast of Beiping, 60 li from Xianghe; Lintingzhen is 50 li southeast of Baodi; Ninghe is 300 li southeast of Beiping; Lutai is more than 100 li east of Tianjin, through which the BeiNing Railway passes, and is 57 li west of Tanggu. From the above, the closest point of the demilitarized zone is only 30 to 40 li away from Beiping. Although the police administration in the zone nominally belongs entirely to our country, the army cannot cross the line a step, and the loss of sovereignty is self-evident. The scope of the Great Wall line was originally very broad, but in the agreement, the range west of Yanqing is marked with numbers, subtly defining the scope of the Great Wall line. The wording is quite clever and must have taken a lot of consideration.

Implementation by Both Sides 92

The agreement took effect after signing. After signing yesterday, representatives from both sides reported to their respective authorities. Starting today (1st), both sides will comply with the agreement and begin implementation simultaneously. Our army will begin to return to Jianchang, and some troops will be transferred to bandit areas to suppress bandits. The remaining troops will be assigned to other defense areas and gradually relocated. The Japanese army will also begin withdrawing from the Great Wall line today.

Acceptance Methods 93

The area currently occupied by the Japanese army will become a demilitarized zone after the withdrawal of troops, and personnel will be dispatched by the Chinese side in the future. Local security will be maintained by the police. All acceptance methods will be carried out in accordance with the Shanghai and Qingdao methods, or a committee will be organized to handle everything. The police in the demilitarized zone will be similar to those in Songhu and will be organized into special police. The number of people will be determined according to the local situation and there will be no restrictions.

Handling of the Rebel Army 94

After the Japanese army occupied various places in Guannei, the rebel army led by Li Jichun and others was very active. Shi Yousan even openly recruited soldiers in Qinhuangdao. Resolving this matter is particularly difficult. The Japanese side claims on the surface that it is voluntary and has nothing to do with their imperial army, and that they cannot take active actions. At the same time, our army is limited by the agreement and cannot use force to suppress them. How to resolve this is a major problem. Representatives from China and Japan mentioned it yesterday, and the Japanese side verbally stated that they would wait for both parties to find a way to handle it in Ping in the future. The Japanese side's temporary goal is only to secure the Great Wall line. It is also possible that the rebel army will be resolved smoothly.

Representatives Return to Ping 95

After the representatives from both sides completed the signing, they left Tanggu separately to report back to their respective authorities. The Chinese representatives, including Xiong Bin, arrived in Ping by special train at 11:30 PM last night. After getting off the train, they went to Jurentang to meet with He and Huang to report on the progress and to consult on various issues after the signing. They dispersed this morning.

Military Conference 96

Because of the signing of the agreement, He Yingqin specially convened a temporary military conference at Jurentang at 11:00 AM this morning, attended by more than 20 generals including Song Zheyuan, Shang Zhen, Lu Bingxun, Wan Fulin, Xu Tingyao, and Xiao Zhichu. In addition to He Yingqin, Huang Fu and Xiong Bin also attended. In addition to reporting on the progress of the signing of the agreement, there were detailed discussions on issues such as the withdrawal of troops and defense zones. They dispersed until around 1:00 PM in the afternoon (June 1st).

Jilin National Salvation Army

Tian Lin's Troops Capture Fuxin and Kangping 97

More Than a Thousand Members of the Faku County Militia Join

Tian's Representative Asks He Yingqin for Instructions

A special dispatch from Beiping reports that after Jehol fell for a long time and Fuxin and Kangping were occupied by the Japanese army, Tian Lin, the commander of the Second Route Army of the Jilin National Salvation Army, recently broke through Fuxin and Kangping again. Tian Yingqiu, a representative of Tian's forces, came to Ping to meet with He Yingqin, the acting chairman of the Military Branch, to ask for instructions. Our reporter specifically visited Mr. Tian to inquire about the process of breaking through Fuxin and Kangping. The account is as follows: Tian Lin, commander of the Second Route Army of the Jilin National Salvation Army, and Deputy Commander Yu Ruoyu, led more than 3,000 troops in February, departing from the Jiangjiapi Gulch base in Huadian County, Jilin, intending to go to the border of Jehol to request military supplies from the authorities and resist Japan for a long time. After more than a month of fighting, they arrived at the border of Jehol on April 1. Unexpectedly, Jehol fell, and the passes of the Great Wall fell one after another. The isolated army was in a desperate situation, surrounded on all sides. In this desperate situation, the only way to survive was to fight to the death. They joined forces with the volunteer army of the Liaoning Incident led by Jia Bingyi and Wang Hanpeng, and conquered Fuxin on April 5, killing many enemies and seizing more than 100 guns and more than 50,000 rounds of ammunition, and two cannon mortars. Later, after several westward advances, they were unable to defend the heavy siege and had to return east. On April 25, they arrived at Yangjiagou in Faku County, where the head of the local militia, motivated by patriotic enthusiasm, led more than 1,200 cavalry to join them. On May 1, they joined forces with Jia Bingyi's 2,000 troops to besiege Kangping. After a fierce battle of five hours, the city fell. The Japanese councilor Shimada and instructor Hirata in the county office were shot and killed, and a pseudo-county chief named Liu was captured. They seized a mortar, more than 200 rifles, and the military prestige was greatly shaken. The Japanese side was frightened and began to mobilize more than 400 Japanese garrison troops and more than 100 pseudo-security forces from Changtu, Tieling, and Kaiyuan, approaching the Tian'e River and Wujianfang area under Kangping County, falling into the ambush of our army. After a full day of fierce fighting, in addition to eight escaped Japanese soldiers and 32 pseudo-soldiers, all the rest were annihilated. They seized more than 500 rifles, six steel cannons, six heavy machine guns, four light machine guns, more than 100,000 rounds of ammunition, and more than a dozen vehicles of supplies. After this battle, the military prestige became even more impressive, and more than 300 more people came from all directions. Currently, more than 4,000 people are gathered, occupying strategic areas in Kangping, Faku, and Zhangwu counties, rectifying the army and waiting for the opportunity to fight to the death with the enemy. The person was sent to Ping to negotiate and ask the Military Branch and the National Salvation Association for orders. (May 30)

Chen Mingshu's Views on the Current Situation

Speaks to the Public in Fuzhou 98

Fuzhou Correspondence, Chen Mingshu arrived in Fuzhou on May 23, advocating resistance to the end against Japan. Jiang Guangding and Cai Tingkai telegraphed on the 25th, opposing compromise with Japan, which aroused the attention of the general public. Chen has now moved to the Pacification Commissioner's Office. On the 27th, all sectors of the provincial capital held a welcome meeting at the Provincial Party Headquarters. Chen spoke for three hours, dividing his speech into six points: (1) From the international situation to the urgent danger of China; (2) The mistakes in the diplomatic concepts of the Chinese authorities and the Chinese people; (3) The impending economic crisis facing China; (4) The organization and training of the people; (5) The current awareness and efforts of the people of Fujian; (6) (General) There is only one way out for the future of the country, that is, the final national independent struggle of the entire nation. He expressed considerable dissatisfaction with the current domestic situation. In private conversations, Mr. Chen often encourages people to be thrifty and seek practical results. Posters have now been posted all over the city, welcoming Chen Mingshu to Fujian and leading the people to face the national crisis together. (May 30)

National Coal Transportation Conference

Passes Measures to Repair Locomotives 99

Beijing News, in order to develop the coal industry, increase production, and facilitate transportation, the Ministry of Industry borrowed 1,000 locomotives and freight cars from the BeiNing Railway, and planned to borrow money from Jin Cheng and other banks to repair them. The conference convened coal merchants and railway representatives to Beijing to hold a coal transportation conference to discuss the entire plan. The opening ceremony was held in the auditorium of the Ministry of Industry at 9:00 AM on the 1st. The meeting continued in the afternoon, and nine measures for repairing locomotives and vehicles were passed. The details are recorded as follows:

Attendance 100

The attendees included Liu Chuanshu, representative of the Ministry of Railways; Wang Yongxi and Wu Tingbai, representatives of the Pinghan Railway Administration; Li Jin and Li Yuanqi, representatives of the Liuhegou Coal Mine; Xu Ganfang, representative of the Lieshan Coal Mine; Tong Yuchi, representative of the Jingxing Mining Bureau; Cheng Dong, representative of the Zhongyuan Coal Mine; Liang Shangchun, representative of the Jinbei Mining Bureau; Shen Yuanru and Wang Licun, representatives of the North China Coal Mine; Zhang Zijing, representative of the Huainan Coal Mine; Yang Yijian, representative of the Yili Coal Mine; Zheng Liming, representative of the Zhonghe Coal Mine; Chang Xuchun, representative of the Baojin Company; Zhang Zhongping, representative of the Zhongxing Coal Mine; Liang Shangchun, representative of the Datong Coal Industry Company; Zhang Hu, representative of the National Coal Relief Committee; Gao Hechao, representative of the Huafeng Coal Mine; Zhu Yonghe, representative of the Datong Coal Mine; Chen Yueqin, representative of the Lincheng Mining Bureau; and Huang Jintao, Wang Zhong, Li Minghe, Liang Jin, Hu Boyuan, and Xiao Kuan of the Mining Department of the Ministry of Industry, totaling more than 30 people.

Mr. Chen's Speech 101

At the opening ceremony at 9:00 AM, Baochang Chen Gongbo presided, and Wang Zhong recorded. The ceremony was performed as usual. First, Mr. Chen gave an opening speech, the gist of which was that in recent years, China's coal mines have been affected by the dumping of cheap foreign coal, which has led to a slump. It is not enough to make up for it without overall planning, so this ministry has convened this meeting. I am very pleased and honored that you have traveled from afar to attend the meeting. The main purpose of this meeting is to (1) find ways to organize coal transportation vehicles to facilitate transportation, so as to avoid the stagnation of coal; (2) plan to borrow money from banks to pay for vehicle repair costs. If this loan is successful, it will be of great help to the economic adjustment of the coal industry in the future. I hope that everyone will express their opinions as much as possible, exchange ideas with each other, and make corresponding decisions to maintain the coal industry. After Mr. Chen finished speaking, he left to attend the Central Standing Committee and was replaced by Huang Jintao, director of the Mining Department, who presided over the meeting and began the discussion until it adjourned at 12:00 noon.

Page 10

Passed Proposals 102

At 2 PM, the formal meeting continued, still chaired by Huang Jintao. Discussions lasted until 5:45 PM before adjournment. Nine principles for the repair of locomotives and rolling stock were passed on the spot. The original text is as follows:

Article 1: The Railway Bureau is responsible for repairing the locomotives (with missing characters) rolling stock (with missing characters) 50 trains (each with 500 tons) to good working order, specifically for transporting coal for export by mining companies.

Article 2: The repair cost for each locomotive is approximately 30,000 yuan, and each carriage is approximately 10,000 yuan, totaling approximately 2 million yuan. This requires guarantees from both the Railway Bureau and the mining companies. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce will borrow from the bank on their behalf. All withdrawals of this loan must be signed by representatives of both the Railway Bureau and the mining companies.

Article 3: Regarding this matter, the Railway Bureau and the mining companies must jointly organize an entity to be responsible for the handling.

Article 4: The repayment of this loan shall be made by the Railway Bureau by allocating half of the freight revenue from the coal transported by these vehicles to the bank until the principal and interest are fully repaid.

Article 5: The locomotives and rolling stock specified in Article 1 must be repaired and inspected within six to ten months. After acceptance, they will be specifically used for coal transportation. Thereafter, all ordinary and accidental repair costs for the vehicles shall be borne entirely by the Railway Bureau. During this repair period, the Railway Bureau should allocate other vehicles for supplementation.

Article 6: The ownership and custody of these locomotives and rolling stock shall remain with the Railway Bureau, but the power of disposition shall belong to the entity jointly formed by the Railway Bureau and the mining companies.

Article 7: Whether the coal is transported to Qingdao, Tianjin, Hankou, or Pukou, and from which mine it originates, the (missing characters) tonnage that each train should transport shall not be exceeded and should be determined by the entity jointly formed by the Railway Bureau and the mining companies. If the coal is transported along the railway lines, this tonnage shall also be the limit. However, in the event of special circumstances such as traffic obstruction, where vehicles cannot directly reach Qingdao, Dagu, Hankou, or Pukou, and the mining companies are forced to use these trains along the line, two tons can be calculated as one ton of exported coal.

Article 8: All freight charges and taxes payable on these coal cars shall be levied in accordance with regulations. If these railway vehicles operate on other railways, the freight charges shall be allocated to them accordingly.

Article 9: All railway regulations that must be followed during the coal transportation period, as well as the use of returning empty cars, etc., shall be the responsibility of the Railway Bureau's Traffic Department, but shall not interfere with coal transportation. (Riri News Agency)

Rebellion of Troops in Western Hunan 103

Chen Wo Agitates Various Units in Western Hunan for Rebellion

Occupies Qianyang, Zhijiang, and Huangxian Counties

Changsha Dispatch: Chen Wo, the brigade commander of the former 62nd Division, commanded by Tao Guang, was a hero of the Green Forest in Western Hunan. He was stationed in Hengzhou the previous year and was instigated to plot something. When Commander Tao discovered this, Chen immediately fled. His troops were led back to their old nest in Zhijiang and Huangxian in Western Hunan by He Jingcheng and Chen Changyou, where they resumed their bandit lifestyle. Last year, He Jian sent personnel to incorporate them, and they were reorganized into two regiments. He was appointed as the commander of the 1st Regiment for Suppressing Bandits in Hunan, and Chen (Changyou) was appointed as the commander of the 2nd Regiment for Suppressing Bandits in Western Hunan, stationed in the seven counties of the upper reaches of Western Hunan, responsible for suppression. There has been peace in recent years.

In early May, the provincial government decided to divide the province into six districts, with two provincial committee members assigned to each district to inspect county administration and reduce surcharges. The seven counties in the upper reaches of Western Hunan were inspected by Li Jue, the commander of the 10th Division, and Huang Jiasheng, commissioned by the provincial government. On the 24th, Li and Huang led six staff members and arrived at Zhijiang County. The garrison was Chen Changyou’s regiment. Unexpectedly, Chen Wo, the former brigade commander of the 62nd Division who had been on the run, had returned to Hunan from Beijing and colluded with various units in Western Hunan and local bandits to plot rebellion, intending to capture and kill Commander Li and Committee Member Huang in Zhijiang, and then start an uprising and plot misconduct.

Regiment Commander Chen Changyou and Chen Wo were originally cousins. All the soldiers in the regiment were former subordinates of Chen Wo, so they had long been agitated by Chen Wo and decided to make a move during a banquet to welcome Commander Li. However, Chen Changyou, understanding the greater good, refused to endorse it. However, his troops had all been won over by Wo and could not be stopped, so he informed Commander Li Jue and advised him to flee quickly.

At that time, Commander Li and Committee Member Huang were holding a meeting in the Zhijiang County government office to discuss reducing land taxes. Upon receiving the report, they immediately excused themselves and left the meeting, disguised themselves, and fled the city, abandoning all their luggage. The staff members also scattered and fled. Only a little more than ten miles outside the city, Chen Wo had already received the report and sent troops to pursue them. Just as they were in a critical situation, Chen Changyou also arrived, intercepted the pursuing troops, and told Commander Li et al. that Chen Wo’s troops were already stationed in Qianyang County, and they must bypass Qianyang overnight and flee back to Hongjiang to escape danger. After speaking, Chen Changyou led the pursuing troops back to Zhijiang and reported to Chen Wo that he had failed to capture them.

Unexpectedly, Chen Wo had already realized that Chen Changyou had secretly informed Li and let them go afterwards, so he immediately shot Chen Changyou to death with a barrage of gunfire, and then occupied Zhijiang County, proclaiming himself the Commander of the Hunan Anti-Japanese Bandit Suppression Army. The units of He Jingcheng, Yao Jiyu, etc., stationed in the upper reaches of Western Hunan, rose up in response, and have now occupied Qianyang, Zhijiang, and Huangxian counties. The Qian Army's Che Mingyi Division is also cooperating, and their momentum is enormous. Commander Li, Committee Member Huang, Zhijiang County Magistrate Wen Yizhi, Qianyang County Magistrate Chen Jishi, and Huangxian County Magistrate Tan Ming have all fled to Hongjiang one after another, fortunately escaping danger. Li and Huang rushed back to the provincial capital on the 26th to report the mutiny to He Jian.

It is reported that Chen Wo also plans to lead troops to attack Hongjiang. The counties in the upper reaches of Western Hunan are in a state of chaos because the province has no garrison and the troops have mostly been persuaded by Chen Wo. He Jian, due to traffic congestion and being unable to reach them, has no concrete measures to take for the time being, but has telegraphed Wang Jialie, the chairman of Guizhou Province, to discuss joint suppression measures, and will decide on a suppression plan after receiving a reply. As for Regiment Commander Chen Changyou, who refused to join the rebellion and was brutally killed, a request will be submitted to the central government for preferential treatment to comfort his loyal spirit. (30th)

Yangtze River Steamship Activities 104

=All Routes Resume Simultaneously, Passenger Ticket and Freight Charges Reduced=

=Warships Gather in the Han River, Naval Officers Rotate=

Hankou Dispatch: The four ships of the Japanese 24th Destroyer Squadron, "Peach," "Willow," "Oak," and "Cypress," previously dispatched by order of Banno, the commander of the 1st Overseas Dispatch Fleet, to Yichang from Hankou for reconnaissance along the way, arrived in Hankou again from Yichang on the 30th, together with the flagship "Atago," the destroyer "Urakaze," the training ship "Koyok," and the gunboats "Toba" and "Hotsu," totaling nine ships, moored in the Han River. Together with the six ships of the British "Bee," "Curlew," "Norway," "Netherby," "Cricket," and "Fowey," the American warship "Wake," the two French warships "Ader" and "Franciscus," and the two Italian warships "Carlo Doldolo" and "Lepanto," they are connected end-to-end, forming a starry pattern. The number of Japanese ships is particularly large.

The highest commander of the Japanese Navy stationed in Hankou is Banno Tsuneshige, the commander of the 1st Overseas Dispatch Fleet, who has now been ordered to be transferred to the commander of the 7th Squadron. All naval forces in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River will be replaced by Vice Admiral Minnei, the commander of the 3rd Overseas Dispatch Fleet. Minnei telegraphed the Japanese consulate on the 30th, saying that he would arrive in Hankou on the flagship "Izumo" within a few days. Banno will go to Shanghai after Minnei arrives.

At the time when a large number of Japanese ships are gathering in Hankou and the new and old naval authorities are rotating, Japanese merchant ships have also become active. They were originally divided into six routes in the Yangtze River: one is the Shanghai-Hankou route, with the "Zuiyo," "Daisada," "Daifuku," "Dairi," "Yueyang," "Fengyang," "Luoyang," "Nanyang," and "Xiangyang" nine ships; the second is the Hankou-Yichang route, with the "Xinyang," "Daiho," and "Tangyang" three ships; the third is the Hankou-Changde route, with the "Xiangjiang" one ship; the fourth is the Hankou-Xiangtan route, with the "Wuling" and "Yuanjiang" two ships; the fifth is the Shanghai-Yichang route, with the "Daikichi" one ship; and the sixth is the Yichang-Chongqing route, with the "Changyang," "Jialing," "Fuling," "Yiyang," and "Chongyang" five ships.

After the September 18th Incident, the business of Japanese ships was greatly reduced. Five of the six routes were suspended. Only four ships, including the "Xiangyang" on the Shanghai-Hankou route, were operating. In the past two months, Japanese goods have gradually been transported westward, mostly carried by Japanese ships. Japanese shipping companies are trying to take the opportunity to resume operations in order to restore the original position of the Yangtze River route. After consultation among various companies, it was decided that from June 1st, all six Yangtze River routes would resume operations, and all passenger ticket fares would be specially reduced. Passenger tickets from Shanghai to Hankou were originally six yuan and fifty cents, but now they have been reduced to three yuan, and freight charges have been reduced to 70% to attract customers. (May 30th)

Photo of Fu Zhaoqian and his wife, Chief of Staff of the 83rd Division of the Army, fighting in the area of ​​Gubeikou and Nantianmen.

Jiang Song

Autopsy in Case of Death from Mutual Assault 105

Fei Kunjiang's rice mill outside the South Gate near Daqian Bridge employed several workers from Jiangbei, including Chen Zhongchao, Ji Jinghua, and Bian Hongkui. They often gambled in their spare time. On April 25th, Chen demanded gambling debts from Ji, Bian, etc., and they quarreled and fought each other. As a result, Chen Zhongchao fell ill the next day and died on May 1st. The factory owner bought a coffin and prepared the body. Liu Jingshou, a fellow villager, told his younger brother Chen Zhongjie that his brother had died from injuries, and reported it to the Public Security Bureau, which forwarded it to the court prosecutor's office.

This morning (2nd), relevant witnesses were summoned for interrogation. According to Liu Jingshou's statement, he only saw a scratch mark behind the deceased's ear, and nothing else. The factory owner said that he had hired a doctor to treat the illness, and had a prescription as proof, and it was not caused by assault. Ji Jinghua denied the assault. The prosecutor then instructed factory owner Fei Kunjiang and the deceased's younger brother Chen Zhongjie to be released. Liu Jingshou and Ji Jinghua were released on bail, and it was decided that the prosecutor would personally go to the countryside on the morning of the 3rd to open the coffin for an autopsy to clarify the truth.

Wu Family in Zhangze Robbed of Large Sum of Money 106

Wu Quangen, who runs a clothing store in Zhangze Town, was suddenly robbed of more than 200 silver dollars by a crowd yesterday (2nd) afternoon for unknown reasons. The family secretly reported to the Provincial Water Police, which dispatched a team to suppress the crowd, but they were outnumbered and the crowd resisted arrest. As a result, one policeman was injured and the crowd fled. It is reported that the Wu family will report to the authorities for pursuit and arrest.

Wuxi

Provincial Committee Investigates Telephone Complaint 107

Since its establishment, the Provincial Long-Distance Telephone Exchange has connected seven pairs of rural telephone lines with the Wuxi Telephone Company. Last year, it continued to connect with provincial long-distance telephone lines and installed long-distance and rural terminal gateways mechanically. Recently, the Wuxi Telephone Company learned that the exchange operators had embezzled handling fees and were negligent in management. They immediately submitted evidence and accused the operators of being frivolous and immoral to the Construction Department. The Construction Department, based on the report, immediately sent Li Zhen, a technician from the department, to Wuxi to investigate and secretly collect evidence from various agencies.

Rural Land and Water Robbery Cases 108

As new indigo is now on the market and the rural economy is slightly recovering, the bandit atmosphere in urban and rural areas is rampant again. Yesterday, two cases of land and water robbery occurred. The details are as follows:

(1) A ship traveling between Wuxi and Caoqiao in Yixing was loaded with goods from Caoqiao to Wuxi yesterday. When passing the Kaiyuan Shaotang camp area, three robbers suddenly emerged from the cabin pretending to be passengers, took out pistols, and threatened them not to make a sound. Then they searched the entire ship, and after an hour, they took the loot and landed.

(2) At the home of Zhou Heqing, a farmer in Furong Mountain, the 6th district of the county, more than ten robbers suddenly came yesterday morning, broke into the house, and robbed them of silver dollars, clothing, leather bags, etc., causing huge losses. They also injured Zhou Heqing with a stick, and Zhou Heqing fainted to the ground. His two sons, Bu Gen and Shou Zuoyou, resisted, and the robbers shot Bu Gen in the chest and Gen Shou in both feet. They were rushed to the city for treatment at Puren Hospital. Bu Gen was seriously injured in the heart and was bleeding heavily, and his life may be in danger.

Both cases have been reported to the county for arrest.

Hangzhou

Fish and Dried Fish Industry Opposes Fisheries Construction Fee 109

The Zhejiang Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce recently received letters from the Fresh and Dried Goods Industry Association of Jiaxing and eight other counties, and the Ham and Salted Fish and Dried Fish Industry Association of Hangzhou City, stating that it was difficult to pay the fisheries construction fee within the specified time and that the public was anxious, requesting that they make efforts to argue for them. After discussion at the meeting, it was decided to submit a request to the Ministry of Industry for cancellation, and to inform fish and dried fish merchants in various places to temporarily suspend collecting on their behalf before the problem is resolved.

Furthermore, the Hangzhou City Fish and Dried Fish Industry actively opposed this fisheries construction fee and issued an express mail telegram the other day, which stated: "All city, county, and town chambers of commerce, fish and dried fish industry associations, fisheries organizations, and fishery merchant associations in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are aware that since the sudden establishment of the Fisheries Construction Committee of the Jiangsu and Zhejiang Region and the Hangzhou-Jiaxing-Shaoxing branch office, notices have been posted everywhere and inland tax collectors have been dispatched to verify and collect taxes, arbitrarily harassing merchants and people. This association speculates that the intention is nothing more than for unscrupulous people to use this as a pretext to collect money from the people under the guise of public opinion. As the name implies, it is to take from the fishermen and use for the fishermen, and it is acceptable to collect fees from fishermen and fishing households, but it is completely irrelevant to traders and merchants. Now the branch office is acting perversely and using coercive measures to force our merchants to pay, which is akin to the revival of likin. This association has discussed and cannot approve it. In addition to publishing a statement of denial in the newspaper, we have jointly petitioned various party and government agencies and have been accepted and understood, and have been allowed to forward the request to the central government for cancellation. All member firms and shops have been notified. Before the government explicitly orders compliance, any fees, whether collected or collected on behalf, will be denied. This matter is related to vital interests, and it is hoped that your organization will make the same appeal and help our industry. Thank you very much."

Nantong

Xiting Police Corps Loses Weapons, Arrest Made 110

The guns, ammunition, and military supplies of the Xiting Police Corps were robbed by bandits. After pursuit and arrest by the Xiting district teams of Jinsha, the original items were found at the home of Qian Jin'e, a widow in Hongmiao Township. The widow confessed that they were stored by Feng Jian. Feng used to be the head of the Public Security Bureau of a county in Jiangbei, and has now left Tong. The widow Qian has been sent to the county government for interrogation.

Rich Merchant Blackmailed, Arrested 111

Hu Zhenshu, a local resident, due to business failure, sent a threatening letter to Ming Yunxi, the manager of Yuantaihe Shop, demanding 1,000 yuan. Ming, a wealthy merchant, was usually afraid of trouble and gave 300 yuan to Ge Jinsong, whom Hu sent to collect the money. As soon as he reached the street, he was arrested by detectives. Hu was also arrested in room 35 of the Zhonghua Hotel and sent to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Nanhui

Director of Education Bureau Accused 112

The principals of various schools and people from all walks of life in Nanhui County accused He Jixu, the director of the County Education Bureau, of using educational funds for personal use, wasting public funds, and deceiving his superiors. They requested the Provincial Department of Education and the County Government to dismiss him. Furthermore, the County Education Fund Audit Committee discovered that the Education Bureau's accounts had overstated expenditures and that the cash was stored outside the safe by the accountant. The committee members immediately asked the County Government for instructions, and it was reported that the county would temporarily seal the accounts and cash together, pending the arrival of the director and accountant in the city to unseal them.

Jiaxing

Road Workers Cause Trouble Again 113

On May 28th, the road workers on the Jia-Ping Highway's East Gate section used weapons to beat the water and land patrol officers, causing the East Gate shops to close in unison. Subsequently, the County Public Security Bureau dispatched a car patrol team and a patrol brigade to arrest ten workers, including Yan Zhiwen, who caused the trouble, and the situation was calmed. The case has now been transferred to the court, which has scheduled a hearing on the 5th of this month to summon the two patrol officers, He Xiang, who were beaten, and Sun Xinsheng, a local notable, to testify, so as to investigate.

Before the case was concluded, a dozen road workers from the same section gathered at Shu Temple one morning, extorting money from the abbot monk Fuquan and beating him severely with weapons, causing Fuquan to be seriously injured. When the patrol brigade received the news and went to the scene, the road workers had dispersed. After accompanying the monk to the workers' location for identification, Hong Daxing, Zhang Xiaoxiang, Xie Chaohe, and others were identified as the extortionists at the scene. They were taken to the bureau together with the foreman Wang Zhenghe for disposition.

Yangzhou

Huiyu Money Shop Robbed 114

The duty officer of the Huiyu Money Shop at the Huajuxing intersection on Fanzheng Street in Yangzhou City reported to the local police on the 1st morning that at around 5:00 a.m., the shop was robbed of 200 silver dollars and more than 700 paper dollars from the silver room, and the robbers escaped through the back door.

The police officer reported the incident to Liao Chuliang, the director of the First Public Security Sub-Bureau, who rushed to the scene for investigation, but found no traces. According to Yi Yiyun, the silver room officer of the shop, at around 5:00 a.m., a robber wearing a felt hat and a black jacket suddenly entered the silver room with a gun, threatening them not to make a sound and forcing them to hand over the key to the iron cabinet. He opened the cabinet and took 200 silver dollars, 755 yuan and 8 jiao in banknotes, and 3 yuan and 6 jiao in small coins, then took off the felt hat and jacket, and left calmly.

Director Liao has ordered an arrest and reported the incident to the county bureau for investigation.

Baima Town in the 4th district of the county was suddenly attacked by twenty or thirty bandits speaking with a Yancheng-Funing accent at around 8:00 p.m. the other night. Wuhu

Disputes over Election of Delegates from Linquan 117

All counties and cities in Anhui Province are actively proceeding with the Central Government's convocation of a provisional national congress, and the initial elections have now begun. Wuhu is located in a strategic location with a large population, making it the premier district in Anhui Province. The initial election is therefore of greater importance than others, and it is also attracting attention from candidates.

Since the Wuhu Party Headquarters was ordered to suspend all committee members, only Liu Yiqing, the clerk, and Tong Daosheng, the secretary, were responsible for handling all party affairs. The initial election for the provisional congress was originally scheduled to be held on the 28th of last month at the Private Secondary Business School of the Chamber of Commerce. After Liu and others made preparations, Zhang Xiugao was specially sent by the province to Wuhu to supervise the election. Candidates lobbied and made every effort in advance.

When voting began on the morning of that day, Wang Zuhua declared that he had discovered that a Li Mou was impersonating the party member Hu Wencheng to vote at the scene. Party members have their own party membership card with a photo as proof, but those in charge did not pay attention to this, indicating that there was obvious cheating. As a result, the ballot box was destroyed and the ballots cast were also torn up. At the same time, there was shouting, beatings, and a general uproar. Several people were injured, and several others were chased, caught, and sent to the Public Security Bureau, but they were all released shortly afterward. The meeting broke up in a panic.

The circumstances were reported to the higher authorities for verification and instructions. Liu Yiqing, the clerk in charge of the Wuhu Party Headquarters, stated that since being ordered to handle the election, he had tried his best to accommodate the requests of all candidates as long as they were within the scope of the law. Unexpectedly, this unfortunate incident occurred, and the ballot box was destroyed, making it impossible to continue the election. He has now jointly submitted a request to the higher party headquarters for instructions and resolution with the provincial election supervisor. Before receiving a reply, the election will be temporarily suspended.

It is also reported that similar disputes occurred in the initial elections for the provisional congress in Dangtu and Nanling counties.

Jiangyin

Record of Meeting of Cocoon Industry Association 118

The Cocoon Industry Association held a meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday (1st) at 2:00 p.m. 26 cocoon merchants registered (there are a total of 47 cocoon merchants in the county, and about 30 registered this year). Miao Shaoqing was elected as the chairman. The following resolutions were passed:

(1) The market will open today (2nd). Latecomers will have to make do.

(2) The price of cocoons is 40 yuan per dan for improved varieties and 30 yuan per dan for local varieties. Those who cheat on weighing scales or manipulate prices will have their business licenses revoked.

(3) All surcharges: The government has already canceled all kinds of extortionate taxes and levies last year, so they will be ignored. The public office donation is 0.3 yuan per dan of dried cocoons.

(4) Business tax: The provincial government sympathizes with the cocoon merchants and levies 0.2%. The public office will collect it together with the tax bureau.

(5) Stamp tax: It will be handled according to the established case and recognized as 100 yuan.

(6) It is too late to rush and install the new system. It must be done next year. For now, we should follow the example of Wuxi and other neighboring counties.

Next, the election of the executive and supervisory committee members of the Cocoon Industry Association, who have long been in office, and the liquidation of the association's accounts were discussed.

Today is the British King's Birthday 121

British Community Holds Celebrations

Today (Saturday) is the birthday of the British King. The British Army and Navy, the British Chamber of Commerce of the Public Concession, and the Indian police will hold a military parade at the Racecourse at 8:00 a.m., which will be reviewed by Major General Fleming, the commander of the British forces in Shanghai. After the review, the royal flag will be raised on the parade platform, British troops will fire a salute, and the British Chamber of Commerce will fire a 21-gun salute. The entire group will salute the flag and shout "Long live" twice. Then, the British flag will be replaced, and the Acting British Consul General Davidson will go on stage to receive the salute.

The British Consul General will receive congratulations at his office from 11:30 a.m. to 12:30 p.m. The Royal Air Force Association will also receive congratulations at its clubhouse. The Public Concession Police Department, in order to prevent traffic congestion at the entrance of the Racecourse, stipulates that after the military parade is over this morning, all vehicles wanting to go west of Tibet Road must detour through the north and south ends of Tibet Road until traffic returns to normal. Only trams and buses are exempt. Furthermore, vehicles traveling south on Park Road south of the Boone Road intersection are also prohibited from traveling south.

Chinese National Anti-Drug Association

Memorial Declaration of June 3rd 122

The Chinese National Anti-Narcotics Association, taking this day as the 94th anniversary of Commissioner Lin Zexu's burning of opium at Humen, has received reports from anti-narcotics associations across the country, all preparing to hold enthusiastic commemorations, and hereby issues the following declaration:

Memorial Declaration of the 94th June 3rd Anniversary: Ninety-four years have passed since Commissioner Lin Zexu burned opium at Humen. During these nearly one hundred years, the enforcement of prohibition has weakened, deteriorating with each passing day. The tide of narcotics and the scourge of opium have continued to grow and increase. If Commissioner Lin were to rise from the grave, one wonders how heartbroken he would be, perhaps uttering a lament about the mainland sinking into utter ruin. Let us take a general look at the scourge of opium over the past year. Who would not feel a sense of national despair and a nation on the brink of destruction? In provinces along the Yangtze River, opium has openly become a public commodity, implemented despite opposition. Along the Yangtze River, steamboats transporting opium have become commonplace, and the practice is escalating, defying prevention. In Yichang, Chongqing, and provinces like Henan and Hebei, illicit drug manufacturing facilities are rampant, with authorities turning a blind eye, and passersby casting sidelong glances. The poison of red pills spreads throughout the north and south of the Yangtze River, like a flood, with few escaping its reach. As for the Chairman of Rehe, he abandons the province to protect opium cultivation, and officials entering and exiting North China cannot do so without undergoing thorough searches. This represents a complete absence of discipline, bringing shame upon the international community. Commissioner Lin Zexu, ninety-four years ago, already lamented the proliferation of evils in his era, causing him great sorrow. However, he surely never imagined that the strange phenomena of today would reach such an extent. What is somewhat encouraging is that the prohibition policies of Shandong and Zhejiang have not yet gone astray, and the Fujian authorities have already taken measures to eradicate opium seedlings. However, the scourge of drug pills in Zhejiang Province remains severe in secret, and many residents of Fujian Province openly engage in the opium trade. Whether opium prohibition will succeed still depends on the authorities' unwavering determination and effective measures to make a definitive judgment. Our association upholds Commissioner Lin Zexu's spirit of eradicating narcotics thoroughly, and follows the late Premier's instruction to never compromise. It is our duty to move forward bravely. As long as there is breath in us, our resolve will not waver. Even in today's circumstances, amidst thorns and surrounded by demons, when the anti-narcotics movement is restricted and freedom of speech and propaganda is suppressed, we are determined to sacrifice and persevere, vowing to unite the strength of the people to eradicate the source of narcotics. We dare to declare to our compatriots that even during this period of national crisis, we must not forget the importance of anti-narcotics efforts. Although enemy guns and bombs can inflict damage, they are not as terrifying as the chronic destruction caused by narcotics. Armed aggression can still be resisted, but the devastation wrought by narcotics leaves no possibility of escape. It is our hope that compatriots throughout the country will no longer disregard the fact that anti-narcotics efforts are essential to saving the nation, and that saving the nation must begin with anti-narcotics efforts. Let us work together to achieve the goal of cleansing and stabilizing the nation, so that we may comfort the spirits of the martyrs in heaven and not fail the meaning of this day of commemoration. The Chinese National Anti-Narcotics Association, with this declaration.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway

Unpaid Bond Interest 123

Investor Association Urges Sino-British Corporation

To Lodge a Serious Inquiry with the Chinese Government

The *Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury* reports that the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Investor Association held a meeting on Thursday at Jardine Matheson & Co., Ltd. at No. 2 Guangdong Road. Mr. Retinil was elected as chairman, followed by the election of Mr. Retinil, Mr. Haygate, and Mr. Morgan to the executive committee, who will visit Mr. Pusubique, the Shanghai representative of the Sino-British Corporation, to seek ways to protect the interests of the road's investors. Before the election of the executive committee, the temporary honorary secretary, Mr. Gu Pei, stated the opinions of several bondholders, saying that they wished to consolidate the strength of the Sino-British Corporation and draw public attention to the road's operations and shortfalls. The principal and interest of the bonds issued during the construction of the road are unconditionally guaranteed by the Chinese government and secured by the entire property of the road. Now, the semi-annual bond interest has been unpaid for three periods, and the net profit bonds have not been paid a penny since 1929. Therefore, it is now appropriate to ask the Sino-British Corporation, as the custodian of the bondholders, to lodge a serious inquiry with the Chinese government and request the fulfillment of its obligations. Subsequently, Mr. Anderson described the initial operation of the road, stating that the road could have been profitable, but due to interference from the military and waste by the Railway Bureau, it has not been able to achieve profitability. Chinese pledges are not worth the paper they are written on and are now worthless.

Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee to Meet Today

The Day After Tomorrow's General Meeting 126

Since the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (招商局) returned to state operation, it plans to expand its shipping business and intends to borrow 360,000 (rumors say 400,000, which is inaccurate) gold pounds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee to purchase six coastal and Yangtze River ships. This has been approved by the Central Political Council. The Boxer Indemnity Committee is scheduled to convene a Finance Committee meeting today at 4 p.m. and a board meeting the day after tomorrow to discuss the matter.

Proposed Loan 127

The board of directors of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company plans to borrow funds from the Boxer Indemnity to expand its shipping business. Executive directors Zhang Shouyong and Liu Hongsheng, along with Minister of Communications Zhu Jia骅, negotiated with Zhu Jia骅, Wang Jingwei, Yu Youren, Dai Jitao, Chen Guofu, Zhang Daofan, and others, who jointly proposed to the Central Political Council to borrow 360,000 gold pounds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee to purchase six coastal and Yangtze River ships. This has been approved by the Central Political Council. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has submitted a detailed plan to the Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors.

One of the Boxer Indemnity Funds 128

The British-returned Boxer Indemnity funds, deposited in London, amount to approximately 2 million gold pounds, with an annual interest rate of 2%. The distribution criteria are two-thirds for railways and one-third for water conservancy. The stipulation is that goods or materials must be purchased from Britain, and no cash can be received. As for water conservancy projects, there is no need to purchase materials from Britain. Therefore, 800,000 gold pounds under the name of water conservancy cannot be used. It must be re-loaned to domestic enterprises that need British materials in order to be converted into cash. It is appropriate to re-loan it to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to purchase new ships, and the company will repay the cash in the future, which can then be used for water conservancy projects.

Revenue Guarantee 129

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company re-loans the Boxer Indemnity funds, the water conservancy portion of the funds, excluding the Huai River diversion project, 360,000 pounds, calculated at 16 Chinese currency yuan per pound, totaling 5.76 million Chinese currency yuan, with a weekly interest rate of 5%. The revenue from the six newly purchased coastal and Yangtze River ships will be used as collateral. Once approved by today's Boxer Indemnity Committee meeting, it can be implemented.

Six New Ships 130

Borrowing the Boxer Indemnity funds to purchase four coastal ships, including three of 3,500 tons each and one of 3,000 tons, and two Yangtze River ships of 3,500 tons each. In the future, the coastal ships will be dedicated to the Nanyang (Southeast Asia) route, and the Yangtze River ships will be dedicated to the Shanghai-Hankou line. All materials will be purchased from Britain. The coastal ships will be manufactured in Britain, and the Yangtze River ships will be manufactured at the Jiangnan Shipyard in Shanghai. The total cost is approximately 6-7 million yuan.

Tax Exemption on Materials 131

Once approved, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will immediately proceed, and plans to send personnel to Britain for negotiations. It will take approximately one year to complete the construction. As for the import of materials for the new ships, it is also planned to request the Ministry of Finance to follow the example of tax exemptions for materials for state-owned railways to provide incentives.

Today's Finance Meeting 132

The Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee is scheduled to convene a Finance Committee meeting today at approximately 4 p.m. to discuss the loan issue and review the loan proposal submitted by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, so that the committee can formulate a recommendation to be submitted to the Standing Committee of the Board of Directors for formal discussion. Then, after a substantial resolution is made, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will be notified in writing. It is now known that members of the Finance Committee have received notifications, and Director-General Hang Liwu is scheduled to come to Shanghai today to participate. It is also rumored that if necessary, representatives from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company will be invited to the meeting to explain everything.

The Day After Tomorrow's General Meeting 133

After today's meeting, the committee will have a day of rest on Saturday. The day after tomorrow, Monday, the Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors General Meeting will be held. The main issues to be discussed at that time are the railway ministry's 4.52 million-pound loan contract and the Finance Committee's recommendation on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company loan proposal. The railway ministry's loan contract has already been drafted by the previous meeting. If it can be fully approved on that day, the contract can be signed in Nanjing soon.

General Meeting Proposals 134

The important proposals for the 5th's General Meeting are two: (A) The Ministry of Railways' borrowing of 4.5 million pounds in British currency from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to complete the Zhuzhou-Shaoguan section of the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, including ① a previously borrowed zero amount of 500,000 pounds, ② current installments of 740,000 pounds due from 1933 to 1937, ③ 1.6 million pounds for material purchases, and ④ 1.2 million pounds in railway bonds issued by the Railway Ministry, plus 100,000 pounds in interest. These four types of loans, totaling 4.5 million pounds, have been discussed by the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Finance Committee for several months. On the 22nd of last month, the Finance Committee also finalized a general contract, resolving to submit it to the Board of Directors for review. Therefore, at the 5th's General Meeting, this case will be at its final critical stage. (B) The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's case of borrowing 360,000 pounds to expand its shipping business, in preparation for purchasing ships, is also scheduled to be discussed at the 5th's General Meeting to determine whether to grant the loan.

Requesting a Ban on Arms Imports into Sichuan Province 135

Japanese Merchants Plan to Resume Yangtze River Shipping 136

Following the recent signing of the Sino-Japanese agreement, the Japanese Post Office in this city has increased its number of ships by eight, dedicated to transporting Japanese goods to China. A ship arrives every two days, and each time, it imports 18,000 to 19,000 pieces of Japanese goods. The number of inferior goods imported into Shanghai each week is at least 60,000 pieces. Many are transferred to the Yangtze River. Therefore, from this month onwards, Nisshin Kisen Kaisha (日淸汽船會社) has begun to reorganize its ships in preparation for resuming operations. The situation is recorded as follows:

Dispatching Large Ships 137

Recently, the number of Japanese goods transshipped from Shanghai to Hankou, Changsha, Yichang, and other ports has been increasing. Each time a Nisshin Kisen Kaisha Yangtze River ship exports, it transports approximately 500 to 600 tons. Although Nisshin currently only has four ships on the Shanghai-Hankou line, they have all been replaced with the largest Yangtze River ships, such as the Luoyang Maru, Fengyang Maru, Nanyang Maru, and Xiangyang Maru, operating three times a month. The import of goods is even better than the export of goods because Mitsui and others package rapeseed and miscellaneous grains for transfer to Japan. The operation of Japanese ships on the Yangtze River is gradually developing invisibly.

Selling Old Ships 138

Taking advantage of the opportunity to reorganize its Yangtze River ships, the company has decided to eliminate four old ships of the Dai (大) class that are over thirty years old and send them to Japan for sale. Among them, the Daifuku Maru, Daitori Maru, and Daitei Maru are docked in the river in front of the Meifu Wharf. The cabins have been dismantled, and wave-resistant bulkheads have been added to the cargo holds, as Yangtze River ships are not suitable for ocean voyages and must be modified with wave-resistant bulkheads. The Daijou Maru will also be modified. After these four ships are sold in Japan, four more ships will be sent.

Dismissing Seamen 139

Among the Yangtze River ships being prepared to be sold in Japan, there are still a group of stokers and sailors, all of whom are Chinese. This group of seamen will all be dismissed after the ships are sold. However, they must sail to Japan, unload the ships, and then return to Shanghai to leave their jobs. Because the sailing date of each ship is approaching, Nisshin has already prepaid all the salaries of these workers in Shanghai.

Building New Ships 140

Japanese merchants have no intention of abandoning or shrinking their Yangtze River shipping business. The company suffered huge losses during the more than one year of suspension of operations since the January 28th Incident. However, it has been able to survive with subsidies from the Japanese government. Now, it is planning to take advantage of the opportunity to resume operations as a plan to make a comeback. Therefore, the head office in Japan is selling old ships on the one hand, and on the other hand, it has been planning to build four to eight new Yangtze River ships to compensate for the tonnage and frequency of the eliminated ships. (Ho Cheuk-yin talks)

China Has Not Promulgated a Patent Law 141

On the 31st, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency saw Reuters reports in various newspapers stating that the British House of Commons was discussing trademark registration in China. British merchants complained that the registration regulations were ineffective and that the procedures were cumbersome. The British Trade Department spokesperson stated that as far as he knew, the registration had not yet taken effect. The reporter went to the Trademark Bureau to inquire about the truth. According to Director Ho Cheuk-yin, he also read Reuters' report in the local mainland newspapers in Shanghai, but the Reuters report in *The Times* stated that the British House of Commons was discussing patent law, not trademark law. Which of the two Reuters reports is accurate, he would not presume to say. Regarding patent law, our country has not yet promulgated any laws, nor is it convenient to express opinions. However, regarding trademarks, the bureau treats applications for registration from people of any nationality fairly and impartially in accordance with the law, except for the Soviet Union, where no trade agreement has been reached. The bureau's judgments on various cases are also based on the law, and there is absolutely no favoritism towards any nationality. Furthermore, the bureau does its best to protect the exclusive rights of registered trademarks in accordance with the law.

Red Swastika Society Burial Work 142

Song Zheyuan Sends Letter of Thanks

During the recent North China war, the Red Swastika Society's relief team, amidst intense artillery fire at key locations such as Xifengkou and Luowenyu, carried out burial work extremely well. They also calmly purchased trees and built houses to console the loyal soldiers. Yesterday, the society received a letter of thanks from Military Commander Song Zheyuan. The original letter is transcribed below for your information:

To the venerable gentlemen of the Red Swastika Society, during the battles at Xifengkou County and Wenyu waged by the enemy army, your esteemed society sent compassionate gentlemen such as Xiong and Xu to provide frontline relief. All the officers and soldiers who died in action were purchased land, prepared materials, gathered and buried in mounds, and trees were planted and houses built in front of the tombs to facilitate spring and autumn sacrifices, and to forever mark the great loyalty of the fallen. It is not only the deceased who were grateful, but also the living who were deeply moved. I, Zheyuan, have failed to serve the country, but I have received such great kindness. Remembering the hardships, I am deeply grateful for your kindness. I hereby respectfully send this letter to express my gratitude. Sincerely, Song Zheyuan, May 27.
