Page 17

Spring and Autumn

Banning Street Guiding 253

— Zhan Lu

A country is an enlarged family, and family scandals should not be publicized, let alone national scandals.

I have seen travelogues about China written by Westerners, which often contain insulting portrayals of our country; or, a photograph of a woman with unbound feet; or, a photograph of an opium smoker holding a pipe; and other unsightly phenomena are vividly depicted in the illustrations, truly ruining China's reputation. Recently, movies have become popular, and foreign film studios often screen movies that insult our country, exposing as much of China's dark society as possible. Patriots naturally feel heartbroken and angry when they see this. But where do these strange phenomena come from? It is due to the unpatriotic Chinese who guide foreigners around the streets.

The Guangzhou Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has recently banned people who specialize in street guiding. Because foreigners come to this city for sightseeing, they often use people familiar with the routes as guides, called "street guides." These street guides lead foreigners to brothels, gambling dens, and various other low-class places, allowing them to take photos at will, which are then taken overseas and displayed and screened in public places, greatly insulting the national image. The Social Affairs Bureau's ban measures are divided into four types: (1) Chinese street guides must register before being allowed to practice. (2) When guiding foreigners on tours, they must first report the locations they will be visiting that day to the bureau and obtain a permit before touring. (3) The bureau may inspect street guide licenses and permits at any time. (4) Those who violate this will not be allowed to guide foreigners.

Street guiding does need to be banned, but can a mere official document eliminate the accumulated malpractices of the past? Furthermore, if street guides comply with the Social Affairs Bureau's regulations and obtain registration licenses and permits, but still lead foreigners to visit the dark underbelly of society, what methods will the Social Affairs Bureau use to intervene?

The lure of money can cause people to lose their sense of shame; street guiding alone shows the lack of moral education. Alas! This is a fundamental problem.

The Flavor of the Window 254

— Rong Yu

These windows are simply as small as a hole. Wherever stations, theaters, companies, institutions, and money exchanges exist, there's always such a small window. Every day, thousands and millions of people come to savor the flavor of these windows.

As for me, I need money every month: I like to watch the hustle and bustle in my leisure time, and I sometimes go out for travel, so I've savored the flavor of these windows quite a bit. When people ask me how it tastes, I say: Sweet, sour, bitter, spicy, every flavor is present.

The bank's window is the most difficult to taste; especially for us proletariat. Several staff members, because they are in contact with money all day long, and money can communicate with the gods, we respectfully call them "sir." The face of a pawnshop employee: the tone of a refrigerator, which is unbearable. In recent years, I have suffered even more, because the place where I work always uses a foreign bank check to replace cash every month. That is not only troublesome: all kinds of inequalities make your stomach burst. Because people wearing Chinese clothes have another window. The check is handed in, you are questioned as if you are being interrogated, then you are given a copper plate and told to wait. Waiting for half an hour or an hour is not a big deal. When the money arrives, it is reviewed again, and then handed to you. Westerners and those wearing Western clothes are at another window. They hand in the check, the staff looks at it, and takes out the money. From beginning to end, it takes only a few minutes. Foreign banks ultimately have a hard brand, full of this unequal atmosphere.

The windows of movie theaters and amusement parks, although they cost money, are somewhat sweet. Because you get a ticket, and there is a lot of excitement for you to watch, but sometimes business is too good, and it will also make you uncomfortable. Our people in this country have never been particular about small courtesies, and they are strong when they start first, you squeeze me, and sometimes they are squeezed so hard that they can't breathe. Clothes are torn: shoes are trampled off, which is a common thing.

The window of the station is full of joy and comfort; and sometimes there is some sourness. Because the traveler takes a ticket at the window, he can travel thousands of miles a day, travel and enjoy the scenery, which is pleasant. The person returning home takes a ticket and sends you quickly back to your hometown to talk about the past with family and relatives, isn't it comforting! However, some people seek food in other places, parents send their children: a delicate wife sends her husband, it's like saying goodbye at Yangguan, and inevitably shed tears!

Finally, I want to talk about the window of the accounting office of this newspaper. Every time the manuscript fees are settled, many pen-wielding comrades stand outside the window. You have a note, and I have stacks of receipts. This small amount, although it is said that drinking does not get you drunk, and eating does not fill you up. | Except for those with special contracts, this refers to our general sporadic contributors. | But the crystallization of hard work is also worth cherishing. The second is the two accounting gentlemen: one young man is flipping through the books, checking the seals: one old man is dialing the abacus, calculating the remuneration. They are also very harmonious and sincere. There is absolutely no face like a pawnshop employee, or the airs of bank employees, which is also something we should be grateful for.

Marriage Agency 255

— Flower Bell

There are already several Japanese private male and female matchmaking agencies. On June 1, the Tokyo Municipal Government's [Marriage Consultation Center] also officially opened. Lonely men and women, if there is a need, just go to the [Marriage Consultation Center] to consult, and then a red thread can be tied under their feet, each getting what they want, and working hard to produce small citizens, isn't that wonderful.

We Chinese are the smartest, and we will learn the tricks of male and female affairs as soon as we learn them. Look, [free love] is so energetic? Going to court for divorce is even more modern. [Trial marriages], which are transactions first and then auspicious openings, have also become more concrete recently. So according to our prediction, on × year × month × day, our Chinese [marriage agency] will definitely be ready, and will be on the covers of various newspapers, with large advertisements, respectfully preparing happy cakes and tea, inviting playboys and famous ladies to come together and celebrate.

We dare not brag about the situation in foreign countries. In our China, we can see it clearly at a glance. On the male side, the ads of [having a considerable occupation, with a good monthly income, seeking a lifelong companion] are not very reliable. If you find the opponent rashly, you will have to eat the lawsuit of [under the age of sixteen, treated as rape]. On the female side, neither high nor low matches, and they become old maids in vain, and their minds are on their feet. It is also improper to stuff the horoscope in people's sleeves. If you randomly arrange a marriage, you are afraid that [there is already a first wife at home]. Left is difficult, right is also inappropriate, so the holding of this [marriage agency] is indeed an urgent task at present, and it cannot be delayed.

This ideal agency is best opened next door to the court. Then, once men and women divorce, they can immediately register at the agency, which is a very good business. But when speaking into the mouth of a Chinese, it is said that it will become bad. If this kind of agency is called a [pimping company], it will be terrible.

Qingdao Mirage Poem 256

— Qing Rang

Competing to say to see the mirage. Suddenly in the tower, nowhere to be found. Pavilions and palaces at the highest level. As if in the vast, cloudless road. What world are the aquatic plants in the water? Coming and going ships, sails open, wind cannons, if you can count. I want to actually find this strange scene. Suddenly, when I raise my eyes, it disappears. Could it be the weak water that sinks the boat, and feathers cannot cross? It is a direct ascent to the sky, only lacking a tired traveler to ride. Even if the Emperor has transcended the dust for eighty thousand kalpas. The startled car and phoenix carriage are difficult to stop. Not to mention that the human world toils in vain to wait for noise and avoidance. Laughing at the general distant look, wondering, strangely floating and obscuring. You must know that there are hundreds of Qionglou Jade Palaces in the sky. Where does the Jade Infant and Taizhen suddenly fall at the end? Even if you step on ten continents and three islands to search everywhere. Where can you find the cloud axes and moon chisels? If you ask who lives outside the nine heavens. In the hidden gold and green buildings, you can hear the jade flutes. The glazed palace sees ten thousand layers in the clouds. Turning around in an instant, the white dog has disappeared. Alas! Do not say that the earth is in vain. The Qingdao scenery also urges change. Try to see Jiqi coming to reflect each other. Fearing to be late, scrambling, as if drunk.

Full Length Novel

The Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 257

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Frustrated words spur a young man to resign and retreat

A warm heart pities a young girl, bringing floss in person

Ji Zhi said: Last time we talked in the milk tea shop, I already told you a lot. Do you still not understand? Gui Zhi said: I understand, you're afraid of offending your brother. If you offend your brother, things won't be reliable. It's not that I'm looking down on Second Master, but if you're always relying on your brother for food like this, afraid to make any decisions yourself, then you might as well just break off all relations with me. Because if you didn't have your brother, you wouldn't have food to eat, so how could you talk about anything else? Don't think that just because you're a Second Master, you're so much higher in status than us. Even though we're not successful, we still rely on our own ten fingers to make a living. If we were like you, depending on one person, it's not certain that we wouldn't be able to rely on them, and we would have gotten rich a long time ago. Hmph, you look down on me, but I look down on you even more! This barrage of sarcasm made Ji Zhi's face turn red with shame, and he couldn't say a word. Gui Zhi sneered: You don't have anything to say, do you? You can save that nonsense about waiting three years for me to deceive others. I don't want to hear it. I specifically came to find you today to give you a reply. Having said that, Gui Zhi didn't wait for his answer and left. Ji Zhi stood in the middle of the road, staring at Gui Zhi's retreating figure, feeling that the back of his head had stiffened, which was an expression of extreme anger. He thought to himself that since he had met her, he had never heard her speak so severely. Today, to use such words to criticize him, she was definitely extremely angry. However, what she said wasn't too much; he was indeed relying on his brother to live, a parasite on his brother. It was right for her to look down on him. But then again, if someone who thought highly of him still looked down on him like this, then the opinions of others about him were imaginable. He absolutely could not accept it calmly and let people look down on him like that. He must exert himself and achieve something for people to see. He thought like this all the way to the yamen, and naturally, he was full of spirit when handling affairs. Hou Zhi saw this, but called him to the bureau chief's office and taught him a lesson to his face, saying: This is the yamen, not home. Those who draw a salary here must be spirited and do their work. If there are people who just write their attendance and loaf around here, I have no use for them. Whoever does that, get out of here. Silk and Tea

New Cocoon Yield Not High This Year 272

(Shaoxing Cocoon Merchants Preparing to Cease Purchases) New cocoons from the four rural districts have been on the market for many days. Cocoon merchants have been weighing purchases for two weeks. This year's cocoon production is not abundant, and it is difficult for each merchant to reach their full quota. Recently, the amount of goods arriving on the market has gradually decreased, and preparations are being made to cease purchases. Cocoon prices have been as high as forty-nine yuan and as low as twenty-five or twenty-six yuan. (Anji Cocoon Production Only Reaches 20%) This spring, farmers have been limited in the amount of silkworms they raise due to economic hardship. The cocoon production of the entire county only reaches 20%. Cocoon merchants have been weighing purchases for many days, with dwindling numbers. Cocoon prices have been as high as thirty-five or thirty-six yuan, and native cocoons at twenty-four or twenty-five yuan.

(Haiyan Cocoon Merchants Insufficient Purchases) New cocoons have been on the market for many days. This year, silkworm farmers' feeding quotas are not strong. Cocoon production is only 30% of a normal year. Silkworm rearing costs are not cheap, and cocoon prices are not high, so many silkworm farmers are reeling their own local silk. Each merchant's purchases are insufficient. Improved varieties of cocoons are priced as high as thirty-seven or thirty-eight yuan to forty-four or forty-five yuan, and native varieties are as high as twenty-seven or twenty-eight yuan to thirty-two or thirty-three yuan.

(Yixing Premium Cocoons Open at High Prices) Cocoon production in various towns and villages this year is still good. Improved varieties are considered superior. Cocoon merchants have been weighing purchases for four or five days, and each merchant is competing to purchase cocoons. Premium cocoons of improved varieties have surged to forty-four yuan to fifty-five yuan, and native cocoons are at twenty-seven or twenty-eight yuan to thirty-four or thirty-five yuan.

(Wuxi New Cocoon Production Abundant, Quality Excellent) This year, those raising improved varieties in the four rural districts account for 80%, and there are instructors assisting in the process. The harvest is relatively good, and the cocoon quality is also excellent. Therefore, a small number of cocoon merchants violated the public agreement and started weighing purchases two or three days early, indiscriminately raising cocoon prices and competing to purchase premium cocoons. After the local Public Security Bureau ordered them to cease purchases, all resumed weighing purchases on June 1st. The initial cocoon price for improved varieties was thirty-four or thirty-five yuan, but yesterday it had already risen to fifty-four or fifty-five yuan. Native cocoons are at twenty-five or twenty-six yuan to twenty-eight or twenty-nine yuan. (Zhejiang Dried Cocoons Trial Reeling Results in Losses) Due to the cold spring and frequent rains in various silkworm areas of Zhejiang Province this spring, early-season native varieties have been greatly affected. Late-season improved varieties are the best. New dried cocoons are continuously being transported to Shanghai. According to the results of trial reeling at various factories, approximately 500 catties of improved variety cocoons yield 100 catties of silk, while 670-680 catties of native variety cocoons are required. Cocoon costs are not cheap, and based on current silk prices, factories are incurring losses.

(Japanese Silk Prices Drop, Silk Sales Also Clear) With the prospect of the United States abolishing the gold standard and the loosening of foreign exchange, Japanese silk prices have risen. European and American firms in Shanghai have been making up for short positions and stockpiling yellow and white factory silk. The day before yesterday, silk price transactions surged, and prices also tended to rise. Yesterday, Yokohama Japanese silk only opened at 840 yen, a decrease of 20 yen. As a result, New York and Lyon silk prices also weakened. Silk telegrams were not forwarded, and the market cleared. Yesterday, only 130 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, 153 bales of Sichuan yellow factory silk, 30 bales of Shandong factory silk, and 2 bales of yellow coarse silk were traded. Prices were generally flat and weak.

Wenzhou Needle-Eyebrow Tea Sales to Europe Still Smooth 273

Yesterday, Wenzhou-sourced needle-eyebrow green tea saw intense interest from British merchant Jardine Matheson & Co., with the entire city trading over 700 boxes. Remaining stocks are almost completely sold out, mainly due to low prices that suit the market. There were also sporadic transactions in needle-eyebrow pearl tea from Sui'an and Pingshui. However, precious-eyebrow green tea from Tunxi, Sui'an, Qianxian, and Wudong, as well as Qifu and Ningzhou black tea, all remained stagnant, with prices likely to fall rather than rise. Donggongxi green tea from Wuyuan opened yesterday at 107 yuan per head pan by the Baito firm Yu Long, but calculated in last year's silver currency, that is still down fourteen or fifteen yuan. As a result, Chinese tea merchants have sent out a large number of telegrams and are taking a more conservative approach to purchasing goods from the interior.

Tea Merchants Prevent Further Decline in Black Tea Prices 274

This year's Qimen, Fuliang, and other black teas came on the market with an initial opening price that was already one-third lower than last year. Unexpectedly, British firms' sales appetite was not strong, and Chinese tea merchants competed to sell at low prices, leading to repeated and unlimited price drops. Based on the current market estimates, prices have fallen another 30% since the opening, resulting in losses of no less than sixty or seventy yuan per dan for the hao firms. Given this situation and the potentially dire future prospects, the foreign firms' Tea Industry Association held a joint meeting of warehouse firms and hao firms the other day to discuss ways to prevent further price declines. It was agreed that prices should not fall below a certain minimum: Qimen tea, first batch 120 yuan, second batch 85 yuan, third batch 70 yuan; Fuliang tea, first batch 100 yuan, second batch 80 yuan, third batch 65 yuan; Qiupu tea, first batch 85 yuan, second batch 75 yuan, third batch 60 yuan. The above proposals have already been notified to all tea warehouses for compliance in order to maintain the foundation of the tea industry.

Forward Flour Prices Increasingly Strong 276

│Tianjin and Shandong Merchants Both Absorbing│

Yesterday, the flour market showed initial flatness followed by increasing strength in the morning session. With wheat prices from overseas down slightly by one or two jiao, the market sentiment was initially not good. However, factories showed little willingness to sell, as the prospects for new wheat are still uncertain. Recently, imported wheat has also not been cost-effective, so in each market, the forward trend gradually improved. By the afternoon session, the forward market sentiment was even stronger, as the difference between near-term and forward prices was very large, and spread trades were active. At the same time, merchants from Tianjin and Shandong frequently bought forward contracts, leading to a gradual rise in forward prices. This situation is quite justified in the absence of competition from imported wheat. Whether there will be changes after the new wheat arrives will depend on the factories' sales. As a result, the current month was up five li compared to the previous day, July was up one and a half fen, August and September were up one and seven and a half li, October was up one and two and a half li, and November was up one and seven and a half li.

New Wheat Enters the Market, Futures Prices Fall Slightly 277

Yesterday, the wheat futures market presented a flat and weak picture. With foreign wheat prices down one or two jiao and the weather turning sunny and smooth, harvesting has already begun in several places in the Jiangnan region. In the Jiangbei region, it will also be available in about a week. Given this favorable weather, the market sentiment suddenly weakened, and the selling pressure from inland merchants increased. The estimated price for new wheat for delivery in Jiangnan is around four yuan (per shi), and the estimated price in Wuxi is four yuan and five jiao. With both new supplies and arrivals strong, there may be discrepancies when factory demand is weak. As a result, July fell two fen compared to the previous day, August fell one fen, September fell two fen, and October initially fell slightly by three fen, but later recovered by three fen.

Ningbo New Broad Beans Open at 5.8 Yuan 278

New broad beans have already come on the market in various producing areas. The reason for their lackluster sales is that the outgoing route is ordinary, leading to a general apathy among merchants. Purchases may only be triggered when goods flood the market and prices are low. Yesterday, 50 bags of Ningbo-broken broad beans, whose quality was quite good, were transported to the market. The Tianjin merchants opened the bidding price at 5.8 yuan. There are 1,600-odd bags of Wenzhou broad beans arriving today, and it is feared that their prices will be difficult to reach the original levels.

Free Talk

We Need a Chekhov 283

— Shiheng

Among the literary writers of past Russia, I greatly admired Chekhov. Because from his pen, he left us countless silhouettes of the intellectual class of Russia at that time—those alienated, numb, neurotic, and nihilistic intellectuals spouting brilliant theories in various settings.

There are more such intellectuals in present-day China than in Chekhov's Russia. However, we do not have a writer like Chekhov, so no one is leaving us portraits of these intellectuals.

Let me give an example now: The other day, a certain dance hall held a ×× Save the Nation cum Celebrate the Movie Queen convention. Naturally, there had to be many celebrities to call for or support the event. But the so-called celebrities were either bureaucratic intellectuals or capitalist intellectuals. Then, a round-headed gentleman came out to give a speech. The gist of his speech was: [Today we are holding this grand ×× Dance to Save the Nation convention. One reason is to celebrate the election of Ms. ×× as Movie Queen, and the second is to promote the ideology of ×× saving the nation...] (Next, he spoke a great deal about the theory of ×× saving the nation.)

But how can dancing save the nation? This eloquent gentleman then gave a personal example and continued to speak: [Gentlemen, in various dance halls, you can often see me (According to those with dancing experience, this gentleman goes to several dance halls every night in rotation). But you don't know that I have another intention. Recently, young people in general are obsessed with Westernization and like to wear Western clothes. But when I go to dance halls, I wear a Chinese-made long gown. So my dancing is not for entertainment. I want to promote patriotism with the long-gown ideology in this most fashionable place...]

[Gentlemen,] I would like to continue what this gentleman said: [Do you think this speech is ridiculous? But there are countless members of the Chinese intellectual class similar to this gentleman. They are spouting brilliant theories everywhere. Are their actions and words not worth recording and leaving for our descendants to see? Therefore, how should we expect to see a writer like Chekhov emerge soon to do this work for us!]

The Fourth Type of Person 284

— Another Realm

Suppose the first type of person is left, the second type of person is right, and the third type of person is neither left nor right (the meaning of the third type of person actually contains a certain degree of left-leaning, but he is still a considerable distance away from "fellow travelers"). Then there is also a fourth type of person. This fourth type of person is both left and right, and can be left or right.

If you ask whether there are currently such people in the literary world who are both left and right, the answer is yes, and in considerable numbers.

The fourth type of person is naturally much more intelligent than the third type of person. The third type of person is actually a fool. The fourth type of person is truly intelligent. They have a skill: they speak human language to humans and ghost language to ghosts. When someone exposes them, they can say: [You don't know. This is strategy. This is for some necessity.] Therefore, there is no way to verify, and both sides consider him one of their own.

The fourth type of person is the pride of the times, because the current era does not allow you to stand on one side alone. Being able to be left and right, able to be left or right, and both left and right, means that both you and I pull him in, and in the meantime, he calmly builds his position and reaps double the benefits.

If we bestow the title of [fence-sitter] on the third type of person, then we can give the fourth type of person the badge of [two-facedness]. Comparing the two, we can know the inevitability of the superior defeating the inferior. A person sitting on the fence obviously has the danger of displeasing both sides. A person who is yin to yin and yang to yang can cater to each side's preferences, as long as they are careful not to mix up the yin and yang sides.

It is said that the fourth type of person is always victorious. I still have a great wish: I hope they will lead China, being both white and red, so that other countries cannot figure out our mysteries. With everyone treating us as comrades, China will naturally exist forever.

Some say that this fourth type of person is not new. They are worshiping bureaucracy as their elder, and are true old-brand opportunists. Whether this is true remains to be examined.

Mother 285

— Luo Hong

Madam was really angry today, scolding her only daughter for the first time.

But the few words she scolded did not move her daughter's heart, but made herself cry. Her daughter is now nineteen years old. She had never scolded her before. Now that she had spoken, it was as if she had done something wrong to her daughter, and she felt so sad. So she cried.

Her daughter had only studied in Shanghai for a few months, and she had changed so quickly. Madam had seen a lot of the world. Although Shanghai is prosperous, many families send their children there. Although some become bad, there are also many who become good, like her cousin's two sons who are so good. One came back to be a lawyer and the other came back to be a doctor, and they did not learn anything bad. There are also bad ones, but Madam always said that they were bad by nature and had never blamed Shanghai for being too prosperous. Now, Shanghai had really spoiled her daughter, and she began to suspect that this place could really ruin people.

Her daughter dressed so beautifully that she did not look like a student at all. Her former innocent appearance was completely gone. She spoke without thinking and was always thinking about something. Her eyes seemed to have lost something, like a sleepwalker.

Last year, when the pomegranate flowers bloomed, everyone planned to go to Shanghai to study and said many great things. Madam thought that her daughter would become a successful female politician, female lawyer, or some kind of writer. This year, the pomegranate flowers at the foot of the rockery are blooming again, and Madam is very disappointed. Her daughter is gradually leaving herself and heading towards a dark abyss. The young girl is wearing such strange clothes and using so much makeup. Where is there any time left to do serious things?

[Mom, you are outdated. Young people always like this.]

These words really made Madam angry. Although she usually loved her, she could not help but scold her a few words.

But her daughter just smiled at her stubbornly. It was as if she did not see the tears flowing from Madam's eyes, and she hurriedly walked outside again.

A Quilt 286

— Jiang Taiwei

[Gui! I don't have a quilt. It's so cold. It's really uncomfortable under my clothes. I see you have two quilts on your bed. Could you lend me one to use temporarily?]

Yes, I originally had two quilts. But since receiving Wen's letter, there has been one less quilt on my bed. I am not a stingy person, and I am willing to share everything with my friends. But after I let Wen take a quilt, I felt a deep sense of regret.

I often think about that quilt. Its relationship with me is really too close. Although it is a very bad quilt, when I see it, I excitedly remember many unforgettable past events.

Since I left my hometown at the age of sixteen and wandered around, this quilt has been my closest friend. Whether it was in a humid and dark shack or on a chilly journey, I always kept it by my side.

I remember when I left home that year, my mother added many threads to the cotton wadding. While sewing, she said to me:

[Gui! Be careful in everything this time you go out. Just study hard. I don't want you to do anything else. Don't get involved in anything reckless. Your parents will be worried...] My mother said, you are a smart person, you know everything!

Now my mother is suffering at home, and I don't care about her at all. She gets up to work before dawn every day. And me? I am still wandering around from east to west and north to south, making my mother worry about me!

I only need to see the quilt, and I immediately think of my mother suffering at home.

Why did I let Wen take this quilt? It contains my mother's best teachings to me, embodying my mother's love, sorrow, and hope for me! I really hate myself!

The day before yesterday, a friend came over, looked at my bed, and asked me with a smile:

[Where's that quilt?]

[...] My heart was pierced, and I had nothing to say.

Perhaps because of my pale face and sad expression, my friend stopped talking about it.

That morning, that rascal came again. [Gui, I'm sorry, but I pawned the quilt you lent me. It was worth two yuan, which can at least help me through a few difficult days. I really had no choice but to do this. You shouldn't blame me, right! I heard you have two quilts. Can't I get one from you? You still have a blanket, right? I still hope you...]

What else does he hope I'll do? I threw the letter away, lay on the bed, and felt very angry.

[You have already taken away many of my precious memories. What else do you want? Do you want to take away even my soul?]

Carrot Top 287

— Jules Kenaro, translated by Lin Qu

This little house, which had been used in turn to raise chickens, rabbits, and pigs, was now empty and became Carrot Top's exclusive property during his holidays. The little house no longer had a door, so he could easily slip in. Some fragile weeds grew at the entrance, and Carrot Top lay on the ground looking at them as if they were a forest. The ground was covered with a layer of dust. The bricks on the four walls looked shiny because of the dampness. Carrot Top rubbed his hair on the roof. He felt as comfortable and at home there as in his own house. He disdained many toys, but he tried his best to fantasize. His main game was to dig a nest in every corner of the little house with his buttocks. He used his palms like a trowel to gather the dust into a circle and then flatten the ground.

With his back against the smooth wall, his legs folded, and his hands on his knees, Carrot Top felt very comfortable there. Indeed, he could not shrink the space he occupied any smaller. He forgot everything, and he was no longer afraid of anything. Only a sunny day would disturb him.

The water in the kitchen sink, released from the hole in the stone trough, flowed not far from him, sometimes rushing turbulently and sometimes trickling slowly, sending him waves of heat.

Suddenly, he received an alarm.

The shouts gradually approached, and the sound of hurried footsteps could be heard.

[Carrot Top? Carrot Top?]

A head lowered, and Carrot Top curled up, pressed tightly against the earthen wall, held his breath, opened his mouth wide, and even his eyes went blank. He felt two eyes searching in the shadows.

[Carrot Top, are you in here?]

His temples swelled high, and he desperately held back. He was about to let out a painful cry. [He's not here, the little beast. Where on earth did that thing go?] The searcher walked away, and Carrot Top's body relaxed slightly, and he felt comfortable again.

His thoughts wandered in silence for a long time.

But suddenly, his ears were filled with a hubbub. A pair of bluebottle flies were trapped by a spider web on the roof, struggling with their wings. The spider slid down a thread. Its belly showed a yellowish-white color like breadcrumbs. It paused in mid-air, hesitant, letting the strand of silk it held rotate in the air.

Carrot Top raised his buttocks and peered anxiously. When the terrible spider leaped towards the enemy, sealed the web with its small feet, and grabbed the captured food, Carrot Top stood up excitedly, as if he wanted to share a cup of soup. But there was no further action.

The spider ran up again. Carrot Top sat down again, and he concentrated and calmed down, engaging in contemplation. After a while, his fantasy, like a stream of water filtered through sand, stopped and formed a pool of water, still and motionless, because there was no place for it to leak.

Glue

Carrot Top heard people say that for bait for carp, nothing is better than cat meat, not chicken, duck, or pig parts.

He knew a cat because it was old and sick, shedding hair everywhere. It was treated badly. Carrot Top invited it to his house, to the little house, to drink a cup of milk. There, no third party would participate. Or maybe a pair of mice would run out of the wall, but Carrot Top should give it a cup of milk. He put the cup of milk in a corner. He sent the cat to the corner and said:

[Eat as much as you want.]

He stroked its spine, giving it all kinds of gentle names, watching it lick the milk so deftly with its tongue, that he was moved:

[Poor old thing, eat up the rest.]

The cat finished all the milk, sweeping the bottom of the cup with its tongue, pointing at the edge of the cup, and then only its sweet-tasting lips remained. [Poor old beast, eat up the rest.]

The cat finished all the milk, sweeping the bottom of the cup with its tongue, pointing at the edge of the cup, and then only its sweet-tasting lips remained. [Are you done eating, all done?] Carrot Top asked, stroking it as before. [Of course, you must be very happy to have another cup; but I couldn't steal the first cup. And, whether sooner or later...] Saying this, he put the muzzle of the shotgun against the cat's forehead and fired. (To be continued)

Talks

Tang Xiangming and Others Piously Recite Sutras 288

— Niu

Yesterday, I saw a report in the newspaper that Tang Xiangming, Qu Yingguang, Fang Shengtao, Yang Shuzhuang, and others in Tianjin jointly invited a lama to recite sutras every morning from 5:00 AM to 7:00 or 8:00 AM, and kowtowed and knelt before the lama.

When I saw this telegram, a feeling suddenly arose in me. I originally opposed superstition and opposed vegetarianism and reciting Buddhist scriptures. Not only did I oppose them, but whenever I saw various superstitious actions such as vegetarianism and reciting Buddhist scriptures, I would scold them mercilessly, scolding them for being unconscious and for being "A-mu-lin." But thinking about it the other way around, it's not bad after all, so now that Tang Xiangming and others piously recite Buddhist scriptures, not only do I not oppose it, but I extremely support it.

Our Buddha is merciful and saves people from suffering, but the Buddha is ultimately otherworldly, not worldly, so he can only save the suffering of the afterlife, not the suffering of the present. If a person lives in the world and feels that it is tasteless and suffers many unspeakable kinds of pain, he feels that being human is meaningless, and he will think of "one Buddha appearing in the world, two Buddhas entering Nirvana." If this life is not good, he will cultivate a good afterlife; if this life is not comfortable, he will think of cultivating a comfortable afterlife. We have lived our lives to this point and can be considered extremely tasteless and extremely collapsed. There is no hope in this life, so we can only cultivate the afterlife. Truly [Amitabha].

But to cultivate, one must first set a goal. This question cannot help but make me consider it for a few days and set down the following principles. The first difficult question is whether it is better to be a human in the afterlife or not to be a human. If one is to be a human, what kind of person should one be? If one is not to be a human, what kind of animal should one be? The following points are the few standards I will assume for cultivation.

First, I want to cultivate to be a person with wealth and power. If I lose power and cannot live in the mainland, I will live in the concession as a comprador. If I don't live in a small apartment, I must live in a Western-style house. If I don't ride in a rickshaw, I must ride in a black-plated car. Assuming I can't live in the concession, I will run abroad and be a foreign comprador. If I can be such a person, it can be considered comfortable. So, I initially wanted to cultivate such a person, but after thinking about it carefully, it's not very appropriate after all; it doesn't look good on the surface. Therefore, I gave up and absolutely will not cultivate it.

Second, I want to cultivate to be a foreigner. But I don't want to be a foreigner from Egypt or India. I am determined to be a citizen of powerful countries such as England, the United States, Germany, and France. I can vent all the anger in my chest, but the people of weak countries have the difficulties of weak countries, and the people of strong countries also have the embarrassment of strong countries. There is often infighting, and you suspect and are jealous of me. In this situation of maneuvering and conspiring, there are also some unspeakable secrets. Being a foreigner may not necessarily be happy, so I also refuse to cultivate it.

Third, I don't want to cultivate to be a human, because being a human always has a brain and has consciousness. If you have a brain and have consciousness, there are always places where you don't feel comfortable, so I am determined not to be a human in the afterlife, just to be a dog.

And I don't want to be a Chinese dog; I must be a foreign dog, because being a Chinese is not comfortable, and being a Chinese dog is naturally even more uncomfortable. I don't want to do it. If I am a foreign dog, squatting by the side of foreign masters and foreign ladies every day, wagging my tail and looking mighty, how happy would that be! So, I am determined to cultivate to be a foreign dog in the afterlife.

Namo Amitabha...

Riddle 289

— Kuang Bei

| Recollections of a Street Sweeper |

[To transform from such an exciting life into this miserable street-sweeping labor, half of it can be attributed to the Japanese soldiers, but the other half can only be said that one's own fate is really too bitter, and also that one is getting old. But, rather than muddling along vaguely in a [riddle], it's better to simply suffer and eat bitterness! |]

A street sweeper in his fifties, hunched over, with gray hair, slowly swept the street while constantly wiping the sweat from his forehead. If he went back ten years, he wouldn't sweat much. Even if he did, he would often let the drops slide down his nose and into his mouth, and a lick with his tongue would only give him a salty taste like drinking salt water. Now, however, he didn't know why bitterness had been added to the saltiness, so he had to wipe it off handful by handful.

As soon as the red light at the intersection turned on, ant-like cars roared into the street, and people on the street squeezed to both sides. He also became lazy and threw down his broom, squatted down at the back corner of the road, spat out a few mouthfuls of white foam, and rested, panting. During this moment of rest, he often recalled many past events:

[At the age of thirty-five, I transferred from a machinery shop to a munitions factory and was assigned to the machine gun factory, specializing in making machine gun triggers. Although I didn't make many triggers, I could make five frames a day. After they were made, they were tested once, and then, along with other guns, they were transported on a small train to the South Station, and then transferred to the capital. Day after day, batch after batch, what was the end use?

Whenever the country was in turmoil, the southern soldiers were going to fight the northern soldiers, or the northern soldiers were fighting towards the south, all sectors of society were inevitably panicked. Cotton mills had to reduce work, and shops had to clear out their inventory. But our lives actually improved, with double shifts day and night. As long as you could endure it, you could work non-stop for twenty-four hours a day, urgently making them, urgently transporting them. At this time, I only vaguely saw that machine guns were a powerful weapon for sweeping fire in wartime, and I knew that they were being transported to sweep fire at the northern or southern soldiers.

Once, the turmoil came even more fiercely. The higher-ups issued an order saying that within ten days, whether it was Sunday or night, the machines were not allowed to stop. If you couldn't endure it, you could freely find helpers, and the factory would bear the wages. It turned out that the invincible Revolutionary Army was attacking, and a large number of guns and bullets were needed to block the battle. On the fifth day, suddenly the pistol factory stopped working, and the whole factory discovered some declarations and leaflets. Everyone was in an uproar, saying that the Revolutionary Army, which relieved the suffering of the people, had arrived. Were we still manufacturing weapons to block the battle? There was only the reason to strike and welcome them.

After this tumultuous period, the Revolutionary Army did arrive. So, a labor union was added to our factory, and everyone continued to live as before, day after day, making them, batch after batch, transporting them to where? For what use? As vague as ever. After that, there were several more tense periods of urgent work, but no new Revolutionary Army came to attack.

Since the Japanese soldiers occupied Shenyang, it was said that the munitions factory there had been burned down, and batches of machinists fled to Shanghai and petitioned our factory, requesting to be taken in. I don't know why, but at that time, our factory adopted a tight policy. Although no news of panic had come about our own lives, night work was of course not needed. When the Japanese soldiers burned and killed in Zhabei, it was our time to be robbed. An order came down to reduce work, and a second order came down to stop work. When the third order came down, it was the end of our lives, and the factory closed.

When I left the machine factory, looking up at the Japanese planes in the sky, desperately using machine guns to sweep downward, I strongly felt that machine guns were originally powerful weapons in wartime. But our factory closed its doors. It seemed that when it came to resisting Japan and opposing imperialism, machine guns were not needed. What a big [riddle] it is. |]

[The riddle] is always a [riddle]. He couldn't understand it. When the roaring cars had passed and the people on the street had dispersed, he self-consciously and bitterly picked up his broom and slowly swept the street.

About [Money] 290

— Huan Yi

The day before yesterday, I received a letter from a friend, which contained a passage: […What I hate most when running on the road are the outstretched hands of the "Begging Generals" shrinking by the roadside. But

Page 22

now? I really admire their perseverance. The art of making people take money out of their own pockets. For the big theme of saving the country through aviation, I did the job of begging for money for three days... I received I don’t know how many lessons, and saw I don’t know how many kinds of faces... Today I know that money is so mysterious and so great...] Originally, bookworms who make a living in books are as arrogant as frogs in a well, how do they know how big the sky is? This is not that I intentionally insult general reading friends, it is really a conclusion of the experience I got after stepping out of the school gate and climbing into this society. What's more, he is a little brother of seventeen or eighteen years old who has not yet left the middle school gate?

I remember that in the reply I gave him, I wrote a few sentences like this: […In the eyes of money, everything in the world can be seen. If you want to know: what color is the world? What does society look like? What is the original shape of people? You only need to look through the eyes of money, and you probably won't be wrong... A coin is held in your hand, although it doesn't weigh much, but if you weigh everything it sees in its eyes, ah! [I really know your hard work and seriousness.] A trace of a smile suddenly appeared on the gloomy, thin, and dark boss's face.

[Oh! The boss knows everything.]

Clearly, this is a seductive and mysterious tone. Of course! The boss knows everything. In a few months, there is hope of adding a little money. The young man's labor is all sold, and the young man's soul is also hooked away. Cough! Some blood is mixed in with the white phlegm. Ah! Work hard, and in a few months, there is hope of adding a little money. The boss knows very well, knows it.]

Cough! Cough! The mouth is full of blood, and some red floats on the pale yellow face, but it fades away in an instant and turns gray and white. The eyeballs have sunk. The body has also fallen down. There is shaking in the ears, I really know it.]

×　×　×　×

[Granny: Please lend me a month's salary, I won't dare to bother you again next time.] Aunt Wang stood there respectfully, trembling, and said to the granny sleeping on the bed because she wanted to borrow four yuan to send her son to school to learn a few words.

Suddenly, the young master who was sleeping facing the inside was awakened, and with a flip of his body and a pull of his arm, he covered the granny's face with the quilt, muttering: Let's sleep for a while longer, tell her to go call us later.

[Qualification] and [Diploma] 291

— Yi Yi Guan Zhu

In the past, during the imperial examination era, a poor boy, as long as he had aspirations and worked hard for ten years in a cold window, had the hope of soaring to prominence. But what about now? The imperial examination was abolished long ago, and schools are increasingly money-oriented, so poor boys can no longer think about such cheap things. Not spend a lot of money, but have great hope?

However, talking again, in today's society, to emphasize studying, it is difficult for poor boys, and it is not easy for rich young masters, because in today's studies, other things can be ignored, but diplomas are important. Without a diploma, even if you have money, it is useless! Not only is it not welcome in society, but it is also not wanted in schools. But saying that a piece of paper is a diploma, cannot be eaten when hungry, and cannot be worn when cold, but it is so precious! No wonder there are people who, without a diploma, want to post advertisements to seek one.

The day before yesterday (the 19th), I read this newspaper and saw this text in the important classified advertisement column [Seeking a Diploma in Law and Politics], which said: [The Wu surname wants to transfer to study abroad and use a Jiangsu Wuxian registered residence as the best. If there are any who want to transfer it, please send a detailed letter with the minimum conditions to No. 14 Zhaoxing Lane, Bao'an Road, Deswei Road. If it suits, we will make an appointment to meet and talk] and so on. After reading this paragraph of soliciting text, I realized that the diploma that is valued by the public can be solicited with money! So, I have always envied people who have [Doctorate], [Master's], [Bachelor's] and other qualifications. Logically, it can naturally also be solicited by posting an advertisement. But alas, I don’t have this spare money, so I can only sigh at other people’s [qualifications] and [diplomas]. Alas!

Correspondence from a Shop Assistant 292

Mr. Editor:

I am very grateful for your instructions in the previous letter—that is, instructions to the youth—at least to me personally. Now I am here to trouble you again, and I hope you won't refuse? Yesterday, I was chatting with a mechanic in the factory and inadvertently talked about religion; unexpectedly, he tried his best to preach [the doctrine of Jesus] to me! It turned out that he was a Christian. Naturally, Christianity is expanding day by day under our influence, spreading to the Chinese mainland. In the sermons, there are often one or two missionaries who deeply imprint [God Jesus] into the minds of innocent children. What a profound intention this is! In Shanghai? Christianity is so popular! It seems that joining Christianity is the expression that people in the new era should have. Is Christianity so modernized? If not, you seem to be lagging behind. Who would be willing to lag behind? Joining Christianity is being aware of the times and keeping up with the times!

He—the mechanic—told me how he believed in Christianity, that Jesus is the Christ, and how Christ healed his years of tuberculosis and got rid of his gambling and smoking... He also cited many evidences, as if the omnipotent Christ was right in front of him! On the one hand? He said that Buddhism is [superstitious] and stupid, and that only by joining Christianity can one ascend to [heaven] and not suffer in [hell]! His words were incessant, in short, he was a Christian and of course he was promoting Christianity. But I think his words are extremely contradictory! Because Christianity has [the Kingdom of Heaven], shouldn't Buddhism be allowed to have [Paradise]? Christ is the omnipotent God, can't Sakyamuni be said to be the omnipotent Bodhisattva? Believing in Buddhism is superstition, but believing in Christianity is not superstition. They recite scriptures and kowtow, you pray and worship, aren't they the same? The same superstition, so who is superstitious and who is not superstitious? However, I think that no matter what religion, at least its purpose is commendable. Jesus called on people to walk the right path and be good people; isn't Buddhism also calling on people to do good? In the beginning, this main purpose was so pure! But the later believers only knew the what, but not the why, blindly chanting scriptures or praying; how would they know that this is precisely because they feared that future generations would not believe, so they used the words of God and Bodhisattva, relying on the ethereal nature to make you believe and stop you from doing evil. Now, with the slightest difference, some people blindly believe that they are going to [heaven]! How could this be the original intention of the founder? As for the missionaries from abroad, I don't know what doctrine they hold. I guess they don't have good intentions. There are too many words, I am afraid it has gone beyond the scope of correspondence? Sir! What do you think, please do not hesitate to give me your advice. Finally, I want to declare that I do not believe in any religion, this is purely to speak from the perspective of an onlooker. It is not intended to criticize Christianity or Buddhism! Please do not misunderstand! Wishing you peace Zhong Xing, respectfully

×　×　×　×

Editor's Note: Religion is something of the past in this era, we know that since the existence of mankind, except for the prehistoric era before recorded history, which we have no way to verify; descending to ancient and medieval times, at that time there were few human beings and it was easier to make a living, and human beings were relatively easy to satisfy with the material necessities of life. However, the evolution of society depends entirely on the human [dissatisfaction] as the driving force for its advancement. Therefore, the prophets and seers of that time created the theory of the second world, so that human efforts could have their goals. Various religions are the product of this; so Christianity has the theory of heaven and hell, and Buddhism also has the theory of heaven and hell. Extending this to all other religions, all are intended to make human beings, in addition to working hard for food and clothing in their lives, work even harder for this ethereal second world. This is the so-called idealistic era.

But in modern times, the population has increased day by day, and the competition for survival has become increasingly acute. Even if human beings exhaust their life's efforts for the material necessities of life, there is still the suffering of being unable to satisfy them. Driven by hunger and cold, they have no choice but to plunder each other, and even with strict laws, it is not enough to make them fearful, let alone the punishment of this ethereal second world? That is, of course, completely ineffective. In this era, [idealism] has been defeated by [materialism]; all religions have become arrows at the end of their flight. Understanding this principle, we can know that all religions have no room for existence now. Then why are churches still popular there now? We should know that modern religion has lost its true face and has become a tool used by imperialists to anesthetize the population and implement their aggression. Don't you see that religion with the same value is gradually declining because no one is using it!

We should now see through the hypocrisy of all religions, overthrow all products of the idealistic view of history; only materialism can solve our lives and point out our way out!

Novel

The Life of the Fifth Concubine (1)(10)(3) (Continued) 293

— Edited by Ling

20. The Beginning of a New Life

This was indeed a new experience for her, in fact, she had changed to a new master. However, what made her happiest was being able to be with Zhang Wenbin often. Whenever Minister Su did not have time to watch her, she would hide Zhang Wenbin in her room, just like a newly married couple, hugging and joking around, which was quite leisurely and comfortable.

Due to these days and nights spent together, she now understood everything about Zhang Wenbin even more. In addition, he became even more unrestrained, talking about everything without reservation. Thus, she learned that he was a recent graduate of Peking University, so his background was also quite remarkable. Now he was a First-Class Clerk in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which, compared to the official titles of the former Qing Dynasty, was at least above the fifth rank. Being so young and so successful was certainly not easy. Another thing that made the Fifth Concubine most happy was that he still did not have a formal wife. Although he had had a sallow-faced wife before, she had died soon after. From this, she thought that if she could treat him well, it would not be a problem, and he could follow her wholeheartedly for the rest of her life. As for his talent, it goes without saying that even during his student days, he had done something earth-shattering. That year, when Beijing attacked Cao Rulin and Zhang Zongxiang, he was one of the most radical. Although it was not necessarily because of this that he became a historical figure, he was full of energy and excitement when mentioning his past achievements. It was precisely because of this that the Fifth Concubine felt that now was the beginning of happiness: he was so young and so passionate, and such a man naturally added a lot of vitality to her life. Thus, she believed that now was a meaningful life.

Thinking of this, she couldn't help but feel very excited, even feeling hot all over. So she walked to the bedside, gazed at his healthy sleeping face, and couldn't help but lean down and tightly hug his head, kissing his lips heavily. A strong passion made her feel an extremely pressured numbness in her heart. She knew very clearly that in the body temperature of any man, she had never aroused such a strong pleasure. A gust of autumn wind moved the curtain in front of the window slowly.

When she looked up, Zhang Wenbin was naturally awakened by her kiss. He half-opened his eyelids, looked at her sweet smile, but turned over and went back to sleep soundly. At this time, the Fifth Concubine could not help but feel a little sad. She knew that this was because she had been indulging in sex too much in recent days.

So she immediately shouted to He Xiang:

[Isn't there more bird's nest at home? Stew a bowl for me properly, and make sure it's clean.] [Who's it for?] He Xiang was being deliberately playful again. [It's none of your business!] She also smiled, seemingly about to get angry.

[Of course it's none of my business, but if the master asks later, [Who's it for?] how am I going to answer?] The Fifth Concubine was about to open her eyes and scold her when she saw Wu Gui running in, covered in sweat, saying: [Quick! Quick! The master is here.] So the Fifth Concubine immediately ran into the room. He Xiang, regardless of the consequences, helped Yan Wenbin up, dragging and pulling him back to his room. Correcting the serial novel of the Fifth Concubine. Yesterday's section ○○ should be placed after section 20 (this issue) because of mis-arrangement. We hereby correct it.
